Jul 02, 2025

Accelerating hardware development to improve national security and innovation

Nominal is an advanced software platform designed for engineers working on complex systems like fighter jets, nuclear reactors, and robotics. It helps organize, visualize, and share test data, as well as build custom applications for hardware systems. The platform aims to accelerate hardware development by providing a unified database for real-time data organization, enabling engineers to analyze trends, identify events, and investigate anomalies. Nominal’s cloud-hosted platform automates tasks, accelerates post-test analysis, and facilitates collaboration within engineering teams. The company recently secured a $75 million funding round to expand its product offerings and team. By implementing a data-driven design process, Nominal aims to revolutionize hardware development with continuous testing and feedback loops, similar to practices in the software industry.

Jul 02, 2025

Face-to-face with Es Devlin

Es Devlin, recipient of the 2025 Eugene McDermott Award in the Arts at MIT, is known for creating immersive environments that bring people together in collective experiences. Her diverse body of work ranges from designing for large-scale events like the London Olympics and Super Bowl halftime shows to intimate projects such as drawing strangers’ portraits. Devlin’s recent project at MIT, Congregation, involved participants drawing each other in silence to foster connection and understanding. Through her work, she explores themes of self-discovery, empathy, and unity, emphasizing the importance of transcending individual boundaries to build meaningful connections with others. Devlin’s artistry reflects a deep engagement with the human experience and a commitment to bridging divides through shared creativity and expression.

Jul 02, 2025

Faces of MIT: Ylana Lopez

Ylana Lopez is the assistant director of academics and events at the Martin Trust Center for MIT Entrepreneurship. She leads various programs and events at the Trust Center and was part of a startup that went through the flagship accelerator program, delta v. Lopez transitioned from a full-time job to focus on the startup and later joined the Trust Center as an academic coordinator before being promoted to her current role. She is passionate about education and entrepreneurship, and her work involves supporting various programs, including MIT Fuse and t=0. Lopez believes in the power of entrepreneurship to change the world and is part of a collaborative team at the Trust Center. Trust Center managing director Bill Aulet praises Lopez for her understanding of students and her creative program development. Lopez describes the MIT community as inspiring and welcoming, and advises newcomers to break out of their bubbles and connect with people across different departments for potential collaborations.

Jul 02, 2025

Four from MIT named 2025 Goldwater Scholars

MIT has four rising seniors who received the 2025 Barry Goldwater Scholarship: Avani Ahuja and Jacqueline Prawira from the School of Engineering, and Julianna Lian and Alex Tang from the School of Science. The scholarships support undergraduates aiming to become leading scientists, engineers, and mathematicians. Each student is conducting impactful research in various fields, such as developing wearable ultrasound patches, studying mechanochemistry, researching sustainable materials, and investigating immunotherapy effects on cancer patients. They all have ambitious career goals and are grateful for the mentorship and support they have received. The Goldwater Scholarship aims to encourage research careers in science, engineering, and mathematics and is a prestigious award in these fields.

Jul 02, 2025

From MIT, an instruction manual for turning research into startups

MIT Proto Ventures launched the “R&D Venture Studio Playbook” to help universities and R&D offices establish their own venture studios. The playbook offers a framework for building ventures from research environments systematically. It aims to address the challenge of commercializing academic patents and make venture-building a systemic process. The playbook outlines MIT’s venture studio model, which embeds entrepreneurial scientists in research labs to scout technologies, validate market opportunities, and co-create ventures. It emphasizes the need for deliberate focus and a new translational infrastructure to build successful ventures from R&D. The playbook includes case studies, templates, and guidance for institutions to customize the model. The goal is to inspire innovation and accelerate the transition of ideas from the lab to real-world solutions.

Gaspare LoDuca named VP for information systems and technology and CIO

Gaspare LoDuca has been appointed as MITâ€™s vice president for information systems and technology (IS&T) and chief information officer, effective Aug. 18. He brings over two decades of IT leadership experience in higher education and succeeds Mark Silis. LoDuca will lead IS&T, oversee MITâ€™s IT infrastructure, and play a key role in modernizing business processes. As a collaborative leader, he aims to shape IT policy and strategy at MIT and support the community’s needs. LoDuca’s background includes overseeing IT at Columbia University and managing technology strategies at Accenture. He holds a bachelor’s degree in chemical engineering and is relocating to Boston with his wife.

Jul 02, 2025

LLMs factor in unrelated information when recommending medical treatments

MIT researchers conducted a study showing that large language models (LLMs) used for treatment recommendations in healthcare can be influenced by nonclinical factors in patient messages, leading to inaccurate recommendations, especially for female patients. The study highlighted the need for auditing LLMs before deploying them in healthcare. The researchers found that LLMs’ judgment was affected by factors like typos, extra white space, missing gender markers, and informal language used in patient messages. The study revealed inconsistencies and disagreements among LLMs when fed altered patient data, with LLMs more likely to recommend self-management over seeking medical care in response to certain text variations. These findings emphasize the importance of rigorously evaluating LLMs before using them for critical healthcare applications.

Jul 02, 2025

MIT and Mass General Brigham launch joint seed program to accelerate innovations in health

MIT and Mass General Brigham have launched the MIT-MGB Seed Program with support from Analog Devices Inc. The initiative funds joint research projects between the two institutions to advance human health research and develop innovative therapies, diagnostics, and digital tools. By combining expertise in AI, machine learning, and clinical research, the program aims to drive transformative changes in patient care. Funded by a gift from ADI, the program will support approximately six joint projects annually over three years. Selected teams will receive funding, access to entrepreneurial workshops, and opportunities to connect with industry leaders. The program, part of MIT HEALS, fosters interdisciplinary collaborations to address critical gaps in health and life sciences innovation.

Jul 02, 2025

MIx helps innovators tackle challenges in national security

MIT’s Mission Innovation X (MIx) bridges the gap between startups and government defense agencies by developing educational programs, supporting research, and facilitating connections among various stakeholders. Led by Gene Keselman, Sertac Karaman, and Fiona Murray, MIx helps startups understand defense customers’ needs and navigate government engagement challenges. Through MIx, innovators receive funding and defense agencies gain access to cutting-edge technologies with dual civilian and defense applications. The program, rooted in MIT’s history of collaboration with the Department of Defense, aims to enhance America’s security capabilities while fostering innovation. MIx’s early successes include projects with startups like Picogrid and Nominal, demonstrating the program’s potential to drive future collaborations and advancements in defense technology.

Jul 02, 2025

Summer 2025 reading from MIT

MIT authors have published a variety of books in the past year covering topics in science, technology, society, education, arts, culture, and more. Highlights include books on the microcosmos and infectious diseases, nature’s wonders, healthcare analytics, longevity hubs, AI for societal good, the impact of technology, entrepreneurship, police reform, letterlocking, the global economy, minority rights, and the evolution of U.S. retailing. Additionally, there are books on fantasy novels, children’s literature, and picture books by MIT community members.

Jul 02, 2025

Using generative AI to help robots jump higher and land safely

Diffusion models like OpenAIâ€™s DALL-E are being used to generate new designs by prompting AI systems to create images, videos, or blueprints. Generative artificial intelligence (GenAI) models are also creating working robots by generating structures and control systems. MITâ€™s CSAIL developed a system where users can draft a 3D model of a robot, specify parts to modify, and use GenAI to optimize the design, resulting in a robot that jumps higher. The AI-generated design featured curved linkages, improving the robot’s performance. The researchers optimized the design through multiple iterations, achieving significant improvements in jumping and landing abilities. The use of diffusion models in robot design could revolutionize how machines are created, with potential applications in various industries. Future iterations could incorporate lighter materials and more complex functionalities, paving the way for innovative robotics designs guided by generative AI.

Jul 01, 2025

Accelerating hardware development to improve national security and innovation

Nominal is an advanced software platform designed for engineers working on complex systems like fighter jets, nuclear reactors, and robotics. It helps organize, visualize, and share test data, as well as build custom applications for hardware systems. The platform aims to accelerate hardware development by providing a unified database for real-time data organization, enabling engineers to analyze trends, identify events, and investigate anomalies. Nominal’s cloud-hosted platform automates tasks, accelerates post-test analysis, and facilitates collaboration within engineering teams. The company recently secured a $75 million funding round to expand its product offerings and team. By implementing a data-driven design process, Nominal aims to revolutionize hardware development with continuous testing and feedback loops, similar to practices in the software industry.

Jul 01, 2025

Face-to-face with Es Devlin

Es Devlin, recipient of the 2025 Eugene McDermott Award in the Arts at MIT, is known for creating immersive environments that bring people together in collective experiences. Her diverse body of work ranges from designing for large-scale events like the London Olympics and Super Bowl halftime shows to intimate projects such as drawing strangers’ portraits. Devlin’s recent project at MIT, Congregation, involved participants drawing each other in silence to foster connection and understanding. Through her work, she explores themes of self-discovery, empathy, and unity, emphasizing the importance of transcending individual boundaries to build meaningful connections with others. Devlin’s artistry reflects a deep engagement with the human experience and a commitment to bridging divides through shared creativity and expression.

Jul 01, 2025

Faces of MIT: Ylana Lopez

Ylana Lopez is the assistant director of academics and events at the Martin Trust Center for MIT Entrepreneurship. She leads various programs and events at the Trust Center and was part of a startup that went through the flagship accelerator program, delta v. Lopez transitioned from a full-time job to focus on the startup and later joined the Trust Center as an academic coordinator before being promoted to her current role. She is passionate about education and entrepreneurship, and her work involves supporting various programs, including MIT Fuse and t=0. Lopez believes in the power of entrepreneurship to change the world and is part of a collaborative team at the Trust Center. Trust Center managing director Bill Aulet praises Lopez for her understanding of students and her creative program development. Lopez describes the MIT community as inspiring and welcoming, and advises newcomers to break out of their bubbles and connect with people across different departments for potential collaborations.

Jul 01, 2025

Four from MIT named 2025 Goldwater Scholars

MIT has four rising seniors who received the 2025 Barry Goldwater Scholarship: Avani Ahuja and Jacqueline Prawira from the School of Engineering, and Julianna Lian and Alex Tang from the School of Science. The scholarships support undergraduates aiming to become leading scientists, engineers, and mathematicians. Each student is conducting impactful research in various fields, such as developing wearable ultrasound patches, studying mechanochemistry, researching sustainable materials, and investigating immunotherapy effects on cancer patients. They all have ambitious career goals and are grateful for the mentorship and support they have received. The Goldwater Scholarship aims to encourage research careers in science, engineering, and mathematics and is a prestigious award in these fields.

Jul 01, 2025

From MIT, an instruction manual for turning research into startups

MIT Proto Ventures launched the “R&D Venture Studio Playbook” to help universities and R&D offices establish their own venture studios. The playbook offers a framework for building ventures from research environments systematically. It aims to address the challenge of commercializing academic patents and make venture-building a systemic process. The playbook outlines MIT’s venture studio model, which embeds entrepreneurial scientists in research labs to scout technologies, validate market opportunities, and co-create ventures. It emphasizes the need for deliberate focus and a new translational infrastructure to build successful ventures from R&D. The playbook includes case studies, templates, and guidance for institutions to customize the model. The goal is to inspire innovation and accelerate the transition of ideas from the lab to real-world solutions.

Gaspare LoDuca named VP for information systems and technology and CIO

Gaspare LoDuca has been appointed as MITâ€™s vice president for information systems and technology (IS&T) and chief information officer, effective Aug. 18. He brings over two decades of IT leadership experience in higher education and succeeds Mark Silis. LoDuca will lead IS&T, oversee MITâ€™s IT infrastructure, and play a key role in modernizing business processes. As a collaborative leader, he aims to shape IT policy and strategy at MIT and support the community’s needs. LoDuca’s background includes overseeing IT at Columbia University and managing technology strategies at Accenture. He holds a bachelor’s degree in chemical engineering and is relocating to Boston with his wife.

Jul 01, 2025

LLMs factor in unrelated information when recommending medical treatments

MIT researchers conducted a study showing that large language models (LLMs) used for treatment recommendations in healthcare can be influenced by nonclinical factors in patient messages, leading to inaccurate recommendations, especially for female patients. The study highlighted the need for auditing LLMs before deploying them in healthcare. The researchers found that LLMs’ judgment was affected by factors like typos, extra white space, missing gender markers, and informal language used in patient messages. The study revealed inconsistencies and disagreements among LLMs when fed altered patient data, with LLMs more likely to recommend self-management over seeking medical care in response to certain text variations. These findings emphasize the importance of rigorously evaluating LLMs before using them for critical healthcare applications.

Jul 01, 2025

MIT and Mass General Brigham launch joint seed program to accelerate innovations in health

MIT and Mass General Brigham have launched the MIT-MGB Seed Program with support from Analog Devices Inc. The initiative funds joint research projects between the two institutions to advance human health research and develop innovative therapies, diagnostics, and digital tools. By combining expertise in AI, machine learning, and clinical research, the program aims to drive transformative changes in patient care. Funded by a gift from ADI, the program will support approximately six joint projects annually over three years. Selected teams will receive funding, access to entrepreneurial workshops, and opportunities to connect with industry leaders. The program, part of MIT HEALS, fosters interdisciplinary collaborations to address critical gaps in health and life sciences innovation.

Jul 01, 2025

MIx helps innovators tackle challenges in national security

MIT’s Mission Innovation X (MIx) bridges the gap between startups and government defense agencies by developing educational programs, supporting research, and facilitating connections among various stakeholders. Led by Gene Keselman, Sertac Karaman, and Fiona Murray, MIx helps startups understand defense customers’ needs and navigate government engagement challenges. Through MIx, innovators receive funding and defense agencies gain access to cutting-edge technologies with dual civilian and defense applications. The program, rooted in MIT’s history of collaboration with the Department of Defense, aims to enhance America’s security capabilities while fostering innovation. MIx’s early successes include projects with startups like Picogrid and Nominal, demonstrating the program’s potential to drive future collaborations and advancements in defense technology.

QS ranks MIT the worldâ€™s No. 1 university for 2025-26

MIT has been named the world’s top university by the QS World University Rankings for the 14th consecutive year. The rankings are based on factors such as academic reputation, employer reputation, and student-to-faculty ratio. MIT was also ranked first in 11 subject areas and second in seven subject areas.

Jul 01, 2025

Summer 2025 reading from MIT

MIT authors have published a variety of books in the past year covering topics in science, technology, society, education, arts, culture, and more. Highlights include books on the microcosmos and infectious diseases, nature’s wonders, healthcare analytics, longevity hubs, AI for societal good, the impact of technology, entrepreneurship, police reform, letterlocking, the global economy, minority rights, and the evolution of U.S. retailing. Additionally, there are books on fantasy novels, children’s literature, and picture books by MIT community members.

Jul 01, 2025

Using generative AI to help robots jump higher and land safely

Diffusion models like OpenAIâ€™s DALL-E are being used to generate new designs by prompting AI systems to create images, videos, or blueprints. Generative artificial intelligence (GenAI) models are also creating working robots by generating structures and control systems. MITâ€™s CSAIL developed a system where users can draft a 3D model of a robot, specify parts to modify, and use GenAI to optimize the design, resulting in a robot that jumps higher. The AI-generated design featured curved linkages, improving the robot’s performance. The researchers optimized the design through multiple iterations, achieving significant improvements in jumping and landing abilities. The use of diffusion models in robot design could revolutionize how machines are created, with potential applications in various industries. Future iterations could incorporate lighter materials and more complex functionalities, paving the way for innovative robotics designs guided by generative AI.

Jun 30, 2025

Accelerating hardware development to improve national security and innovation

Nominal is an advanced software platform designed for engineers working on complex systems like fighter jets, nuclear reactors, and robotics. It helps organize, visualize, and share test data, as well as build custom applications for hardware systems. The platform aims to accelerate hardware development by providing a unified database for real-time data organization, enabling engineers to analyze trends, identify events, and investigate anomalies. Nominal’s cloud-hosted platform automates tasks, accelerates post-test analysis, and facilitates collaboration within engineering teams. The company recently secured a $75 million funding round to expand its product offerings and team. By implementing a data-driven design process, Nominal aims to revolutionize hardware development with continuous testing and feedback loops, similar to practices in the software industry.

Jun 30, 2025

Face-to-face with Es Devlin

Es Devlin, recipient of the 2025 Eugene McDermott Award in the Arts at MIT, is known for creating immersive environments that bring people together in collective experiences. Her diverse body of work ranges from designing for large-scale events like the London Olympics and Super Bowl halftime shows to intimate projects such as drawing strangers’ portraits. Devlin’s recent project at MIT, Congregation, involved participants drawing each other in silence to foster connection and understanding. Through her work, she explores themes of self-discovery, empathy, and unity, emphasizing the importance of transcending individual boundaries to build meaningful connections with others. Devlin’s artistry reflects a deep engagement with the human experience and a commitment to bridging divides through shared creativity and expression.

Jun 30, 2025

Faces of MIT: Ylana Lopez

Ylana Lopez is the assistant director of academics and events at the Martin Trust Center for MIT Entrepreneurship. She leads various programs and events at the Trust Center and was part of a startup that went through the flagship accelerator program, delta v. Lopez transitioned from a full-time job to focus on the startup and later joined the Trust Center as an academic coordinator before being promoted to her current role. She is passionate about education and entrepreneurship, and her work involves supporting various programs, including MIT Fuse and t=0. Lopez believes in the power of entrepreneurship to change the world and is part of a collaborative team at the Trust Center. Trust Center managing director Bill Aulet praises Lopez for her understanding of students and her creative program development. Lopez describes the MIT community as inspiring and welcoming, and advises newcomers to break out of their bubbles and connect with people across different departments for potential collaborations.

Jun 30, 2025

Four from MIT named 2025 Goldwater Scholars

MIT has four rising seniors who received the 2025 Barry Goldwater Scholarship: Avani Ahuja and Jacqueline Prawira from the School of Engineering, and Julianna Lian and Alex Tang from the School of Science. The scholarships support undergraduates aiming to become leading scientists, engineers, and mathematicians. Each student is conducting impactful research in various fields, such as developing wearable ultrasound patches, studying mechanochemistry, researching sustainable materials, and investigating immunotherapy effects on cancer patients. They all have ambitious career goals and are grateful for the mentorship and support they have received. The Goldwater Scholarship aims to encourage research careers in science, engineering, and mathematics and is a prestigious award in these fields.

Jun 30, 2025

From MIT, an instruction manual for turning research into startups

MIT Proto Ventures launched the “R&D Venture Studio Playbook” to help universities and R&D offices establish their own venture studios. The playbook offers a framework for building ventures from research environments systematically. It aims to address the challenge of commercializing academic patents and make venture-building a systemic process. The playbook outlines MIT’s venture studio model, which embeds entrepreneurial scientists in research labs to scout technologies, validate market opportunities, and co-create ventures. It emphasizes the need for deliberate focus and a new translational infrastructure to build successful ventures from R&D. The playbook includes case studies, templates, and guidance for institutions to customize the model. The goal is to inspire innovation and accelerate the transition of ideas from the lab to real-world solutions.

Gaspare LoDuca named VP for information systems and technology and CIO

Gaspare LoDuca has been appointed as MITâ€™s vice president for information systems and technology (IS&T) and chief information officer, effective Aug. 18. He brings over two decades of IT leadership experience in higher education and succeeds Mark Silis. LoDuca will lead IS&T, oversee MITâ€™s IT infrastructure, and play a key role in modernizing business processes. As a collaborative leader, he aims to shape IT policy and strategy at MIT and support the community’s needs. LoDuca’s background includes overseeing IT at Columbia University and managing technology strategies at Accenture. He holds a bachelor’s degree in chemical engineering and is relocating to Boston with his wife.

Jun 30, 2025

LLMs factor in unrelated information when recommending medical treatments

MIT researchers conducted a study showing that large language models (LLMs) used for treatment recommendations in healthcare can be influenced by nonclinical factors in patient messages, leading to inaccurate recommendations, especially for female patients. The study highlighted the need for auditing LLMs before deploying them in healthcare. The researchers found that LLMs’ judgment was affected by factors like typos, extra white space, missing gender markers, and informal language used in patient messages. The study revealed inconsistencies and disagreements among LLMs when fed altered patient data, with LLMs more likely to recommend self-management over seeking medical care in response to certain text variations. These findings emphasize the importance of rigorously evaluating LLMs before using them for critical healthcare applications.

Jun 30, 2025

MIT and Mass General Brigham launch joint seed program to accelerate innovations in health

MIT and Mass General Brigham have launched the MIT-MGB Seed Program with support from Analog Devices Inc. The initiative funds joint research projects between the two institutions to advance human health research and develop innovative therapies, diagnostics, and digital tools. By combining expertise in AI, machine learning, and clinical research, the program aims to drive transformative changes in patient care. Funded by a gift from ADI, the program will support approximately six joint projects annually over three years. Selected teams will receive funding, access to entrepreneurial workshops, and opportunities to connect with industry leaders. The program, part of MIT HEALS, fosters interdisciplinary collaborations to address critical gaps in health and life sciences innovation.

Jun 30, 2025

MIx helps innovators tackle challenges in national security

MIT’s Mission Innovation X (MIx) bridges the gap between startups and government defense agencies by developing educational programs, supporting research, and facilitating connections among various stakeholders. Led by Gene Keselman, Sertac Karaman, and Fiona Murray, MIx helps startups understand defense customers’ needs and navigate government engagement challenges. Through MIx, innovators receive funding and defense agencies gain access to cutting-edge technologies with dual civilian and defense applications. The program, rooted in MIT’s history of collaboration with the Department of Defense, aims to enhance America’s security capabilities while fostering innovation. MIx’s early successes include projects with startups like Picogrid and Nominal, demonstrating the program’s potential to drive future collaborations and advancements in defense technology.

QS ranks MIT the worldâ€™s No. 1 university for 2025-26

MIT has been named the world’s top university by the QS World University Rankings for the 14th consecutive year. The rankings are based on factors such as academic reputation, employer reputation, and student-to-faculty ratio. MIT was also ranked first in 11 subject areas and second in seven subject areas.

Jun 30, 2025

Summer 2025 reading from MIT

MIT authors have published a variety of books in the past year covering topics in science, technology, society, education, arts, culture, and more. Highlights include books on the microcosmos and infectious diseases, nature’s wonders, healthcare analytics, longevity hubs, AI for societal good, the impact of technology, entrepreneurship, police reform, letterlocking, the global economy, minority rights, and the evolution of U.S. retailing. Additionally, there are books on fantasy novels, children’s literature, and picture books by MIT community members.

Jun 30, 2025

Using generative AI to help robots jump higher and land safely

Diffusion models like OpenAIâ€™s DALL-E are being used to generate new designs by prompting AI systems to create images, videos, or blueprints. Generative artificial intelligence (GenAI) models are also creating working robots by generating structures and control systems. MITâ€™s CSAIL developed a system where users can draft a 3D model of a robot, specify parts to modify, and use GenAI to optimize the design, resulting in a robot that jumps higher. The AI-generated design featured curved linkages, improving the robot’s performance. The researchers optimized the design through multiple iterations, achieving significant improvements in jumping and landing abilities. The use of diffusion models in robot design could revolutionize how machines are created, with potential applications in various industries. Future iterations could incorporate lighter materials and more complex functionalities, paving the way for innovative robotics designs guided by generative AI.
